[قوله: هذا ... الخ؛ يعني ثبوت نسب ذلك الولد من البائع، وأمته تلك. منح الغفار. في جامع الرموز. وكذا لو ادعاه بعد موت الأم بخلاف موت الولد (وكذا لو ادعاء بعد موت الأم بخلاف موت الولد): يعني إن ماتت الأمة والولد حي فادعاه البائع، وقد جاءت به لأقل من ستة أشهر يثبت النسب منه، وإن مات الولد لا؛ لأن الولد أصل في ثبوت النسب، قال: «أعتقها ولدها» الجارية، وفسخ البيع ورد الثمن قولنا: وهو استحسان، وقال زفر والشافعي، وهو القياس: إن دعوة البائع باطلة؛ لأن إقدامه على البيع دليل على أن الحمل ليس منه، إذ البيع منه اعتراف بأنها أمته. فإن المسلم لا يباشر الباطل ظاهراً، فصار في دعواه مناقضاً وساعياً في نقص ما تم من جهة، وهو البيع، فلا يقبل؛ لأن التناقض يبطل الدعوى، فصار هذا بمنزلة ما إذا ادعاه أبو البائع، أو ادعى البائع اعتاقها أو تدبيرها قبل البيع. ووجه الاستحسان: إن مبنى النسب على الخفاء؛ ولأن الإنسان قد لا يعلم أن يكون العلوق منه، ولم يتبين له أنه منه، وإذا كان بناء النسب على الخفاء، فيعفى فيه التناقض، ولا يمنع صحة الدعوى. ألا ترى أن الزوج إذا أكذب نفسه بعد قضاء القاضي بنفي النسب باللعان، يثبت منه النسب، أو يبطل حكم الحاكم، ولا ينظر إلى التناقض لمكان الخفاء في أمر العلوق، وحين يعفي فيه التناقض فتقبل دعوته قطعاً إذا تيقن بالعلوق في ملكه وذلك بالولادة لأقل من نصف حول؛ لأنه بمنزلة إقامة البينة. بخلاف دعوى الإعتاق والتدبير بعد البيع؛ لأنه فعل نفسه فلا يخفى عليه، فلا يعفي فيه التناقض، وإذا صحت الدعوى استندت إلى وقت العلوق، فيظهر أنه باع أم ولده، فيفسخ البيع؛ لعدم جواز بيعها، ويرد الثمن؛ لأن سلامة الثمن بينة على سلامة المبيع، بخلاف دعوى أب البائع؛ لعدم انعقاد البيع على ملكه إذ كان له حق التملك على ولده، وقد زال ذلك بالبيع. [قوله: لأن الولد أصل ... الخ]
Chapter of Claims / Section on Claim of Lineage. The seller - the child establishes his lineage from him and her being an umm walad, and the sale is annulled, and the price is returned, even if the buyer claims him along with his claim or after it. This is according to us. According to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, his claim is invalid because the sale is an acknowledgment from him that she is a slave, so by the claim he becomes contradictory. Our proof: Conception is a hidden matter, so contradiction is excused therein, and the fact that the conception occurred in the seller's hand indicates that it is from him. He only said: 'even if the buyer claims him along with his claim or after it' so that if the buyer claimed before the seller's claim, it will be established from the buyer, and it is assumed that the buyer married her and impregnated her, then bought her. One type: claim of istilad (that the conception occurred in the claimant's ownership). The second: claim of tahrir (that the conception did not occur in the claimant's ownership). The first is more deserving because it is earlier, being based on the time of conception, while the claim of tahrir is limited to the present. Likewise, if he claims after the mother's death, unlike the death of the child. Meaning: if the mother dies and the child is alive, and the seller claims him and she gave birth to him within less than six months, the lineage is established from him. If the child dies, no, because the child is the origin in establishing lineage. He said: 'Her child frees her' - the slave girl, and the sale is annulled and the price returned. Our position: it is istihsan. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said, and it is qiyas, that the seller's claim is invalid because his proceeding with the sale indicates that the pregnancy is not from him, since the sale is an acknowledgment from him that she is his slave. Indeed, a Muslim does not openly carry out an invalid act, so he becomes in his claim contradictory and attempting to undo what was completed from one aspect, namely the sale. Therefore it is not accepted because contradiction invalidates the claim. This is like the case where the seller's father claims him, or the seller claims her emancipation or tadbir before the sale. The basis of istihsan: Lineage is built on hiddenness, and because a person may not know that the conception is from him and it is not evident to him that it is from him. Since lineage is built on hiddenness, contradiction is excused therein, and it does not prevent the validity of the claim. Do you not see that the husband, if he contradicts himself after the judge's ruling of disownment by li'an, the lineage is established from him, and the judge's ruling is nullified, and contradiction is not considered due to the hiddenness in the matter of conception? When contradiction is excused, his claim is accepted definitively if he is certain of the conception in his ownership, and that is by birth within less than six months because it is like establishing evidence. Unlike the claim of emancipation and tadbir after the sale, because that is his own action, which is not hidden from him, so contradiction is not excused therein. If the claim is valid, it goes back to the time of conception, so it becomes clear that he sold his umm walad, so the sale is annulled because it is impermissible to sell her, and the price is returned because the safety of the price indicates the safety of the sold item. Unlike the claim of the seller's father, because the sale was not concluded on his property since he had a right of ownership over his child, and that right ceased with the sale.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on claims (da'wa) addresses a specific scenario: a person sells a female slave, she later gives birth, and then the seller claims the child is his own (i.e., the slave was his umm walad). The passage presents the Hanafi position (based on istihsan) and contrasts it with the positions of Zufar and al-Shafi'i (based on qiyas).

The Hanafi ruling is that the seller's claim is accepted: the child's lineage is established from him, the slave becomes an umm walad, and the sale is annulled with the price returned. This applies even if the buyer also claims the child, but only if the buyer's claim is simultaneous or subsequent to the seller's. If the buyer claims first, the child's lineage is established from the buyer, and the seller's claim is ineffective.

The proof of the Hanafi school is istihsan: lineage is built on hidden matters (mabna al-nasab 'ala al-khafa'). Conception is a private event, and a person may not initially know that a pregnancy is from him. Therefore, the apparent contradiction between selling the slave and later claiming the child as his own is excused. This is supported by the analogy of a husband who disowns a child through li'an but then retracts his disownment: the lineage is re-established despite the contradiction.

The opponents (Zufar and al-Shafi'i) argue by qiyas: the seller's act of selling is an explicit acknowledgment that the slave is his property and that any pregnancy is not from him. Since a Muslim would not sell his own umm walad, the subsequent claim is contradictory and invalid. They compare it to a claim of emancipation or tadbir after a sale, which is likewise rejected.

The Hanafi response distinguishes between matters that are hidden (like paternity) and those that are manifest (like one's own actions). In hidden matters, contradiction is excused; in manifest matters, it is not.

The passage also discusses special cases: if the mother dies but the child lives, the seller's claim is accepted (if the child is born within six months). If the child dies, the claim is not accepted because the child is the origin of lineage. Additionally, the claim of the seller's father is not accepted because the father had no ownership at the time of sale.

In summary, the Hanafi school prioritizes istihsan over qiyas in matters of lineage due to the inherent hiddenness of paternity, allowing the seller's claim to override the apparent contradiction of the sale.

Key Terms
دعوى (da'wa): A legal claim or assertion, here specifically a claim of lineage (paternity).
العلوق (al-'uluq): Conception or pregnancy; the moment when the child is conceived.
استيلاد (istilad): A claim of paternity based on the child being conceived while the mother was owned by the claimant.
تحرير (tahrir): A claim that a living child is free and that the claimant is the father, but without the conception occurring in his ownership.
أم الولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, thereby acquiring certain rights (cannot be sold, becomes free upon master's death).
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling based on hidden or exceptional circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a seller claims a child as his own after selling a female slave, and the buyer also claims the child at the same time?
A) The seller's claim prevails because it is based on istilad, which refers back to the time of conception.
B) The buyer's claim prevails because the child is in his possession.
C) The seller's claim is invalid due to contradiction with the sale.
D) The child is declared free and belongs to neither.

Key Takeaway
In hidden matters like paternity, apparent contradiction is excused, allowing the seller's claim to override the sale and establish lineage.

Establishing Lineage of Twins through Shared Conception
Ruling and proof: selling one twin and claiming the other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the legal reasoning (talil) for establishing the lineage of both twins when one is sold and the other claimed.

Core Idea
If one twin is proven to be a man's child, the other must also be his because they share one conception and birth within six months.

This passage from `Umdat al-Ri'aya explores a specific scenario where lineage determination interacts with sale and freeing. Understanding the biological and legal basis for linking twins' lineages is essential for applying Hanafi rules on nasab. The reasoning (talil) uses established principles about minimum pregnancy duration and uterine closure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Ruling
Read the matn: a man sells one of his twins to a buyer who frees him; later the seller claims the other twin. The ruling is that both twins' lineages are established from the seller and the buyer's freeing is void.
2
Extract the Central Proof (Dalil)
The proof is the necessity: 'from the necessity of establishing the lineage of one is the establishment of the other's lineage'. This is because twins are created from one water (one conception).
3
Understand the Subsidiary Proofs
Two sub-proofs: (1) There is no valid pregnancy under six months, so the second twin cannot be conceived after the first's birth. (2) The womb closes during pregnancy, preventing a second separate conception.
These are based on established Hanafi medical-legal knowledge.
4
Define Twins Linguistically
The commentary defines 'twins' (taw'amān) as two children from one pregnancy, with births less than six months apart. This reinforces the biological unity.
The term is derived from al-Misbah al-Munir.
5
Apply to the Case
Since the seller's claim of one twin is accepted, the other twin must also be his because they are from the same conception. The buyer's freeing is void because the child was not the buyer's property to free.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو باع أحد توأمين ولدا عنده ، وأعتقه مشتريه ، ثُمَّ ادعى البائع الآخر ثبت نسبهما منه، وبطل عتق المشتري ؛ لأن من ضرورة ثبوتِ نسب أحدهما ثبوت نسب الآخر، والتوأمان : ولدان بين ولادتهما أقل من ستَّةِ أشهر. قوله : لأن من ضرورة ثبوت.... الخ ؛ تقريره : إن التوأمين خُلقا من ماء واحد، فثبوت نسب أحدهما يستلزم ثبوت نسب الآخر ؛ لأنَّ التوأمين ولدان بين ولادتهما أقلّ من ستة أشهر، فلا يتصور علوق الثاني حادثاً بعد ولادة الأول؛ لأنه لا حبل لأقل من ستة أشهر، ولا يتصور علوقُ الثاني على علوق الأوّل ؛ لأن المرأة إذا حبلت ينسد فم رحمها ولا ينفتح إلا لخروج الولد. قوله : والتوأمان ; التوأم اسم لولد يكون معه آخر في بطن واحد، لا يقال : توأم إلا لأحدهما، وهو فُوعَل، والأنثى توأمه وزان جوهر وجوهرة، والولدان توأمان ، والجمع توأم وتوائم ، وزان دخان، وأتأمت المرأة وزان أكرمت : وضعت اثنين من حمل واحد ، فهي متئم بغير هاء. كذا في المصباح المنير.
And if someone sold one of twins who was born to him, and the buyer freed him, then the seller claimed the other, so both lineages are established from him, and the buyer's freeing is void; because from the necessity of establishing the lineage of one is the establishment of the other's lineage. And twins: two children between whose births is less than six months. His statement: 'because from the necessity of establishment... etc.'; its explanation: Indeed twins are created from one water, so establishment of the lineage of one necessitates establishment of the other's lineage; because twins are two children between whose births is less than six months, so it is not conceivable that the second be conceived after the birth of the first; because there is no pregnancy for less than six months, nor is it conceivable that the second be conceived upon the first's conception; because when a woman becomes pregnant, the mouth of her womb closes and does not open except for the exit of the child. His statement: 'and twins'; twin is a name for a child with whom is another in one belly; it is not called twin except for one of them; it is fu'al, and the female is tu'ama like jawhar and jawhara; the two are twin; the plural is tu'am and tawa'im, like dukhan; and ata'amat al-mar'ah like akramat: she gave birth to two from one pregnancy; so she is muti'im without a taa marbuta. That is from al-Misbah al-Munir.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on the establishment of lineage for twins. The matn states that if a person sells one of his twin children who is in his custody, and the buyer frees that child, then later the seller claims the other twin, both twins are confirmed as his children and the buyer's freeing is invalidated. The reasoning (talil) is that from the necessity of establishing the lineage of one twin, the other's lineage is also established because twins are conceived from a single act of intercourse and are born within less than six months of each other. Since a woman cannot become pregnant with a second child while already pregnant (the cervix closes), and there is no valid pregnancy under six months, the second twin cannot be attributed to a later conception. Therefore, if one twin is proven to be the seller's child, the other must also be his. The commentary then provides a linguistic definition of 'twins' (توأمان) from al-Misbah al-Munir, explaining that the word refers to two children from one pregnancy, with specific grammatical forms.

Key Terms
توأمان (taw'amān): Two children from one pregnancy with less than six months between births.
علوق (alūq): Conception; the beginning of pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school rule that claiming one twin establishes both lineages?
A) Because the buyer's freeing is void by default.
B) Because twins are created from one water and their births are less than six months apart.
C) Because the seller's claim is an acknowledgment (iqrar) that is binding on both.
D) Because the first twin's freeing implies ownership of both.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the lineage of twins is inseparably linked due to their shared conception, so claiming one establishes the other.

Effect of Denial on Acknowledgment of Lineage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on denial of paternity after prior acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa holds that prior acknowledgment of a boy as Zayd's son prevents the claimant from establishing paternity when Zayd denies, and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of lineage is revocable by rejection — once the acknowledged party denies, the acknowledgment is nullified.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of Zayd's denial on a claimant's subsequent claim of paternity. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the ruling and its underlying reasoning, focusing on the principle that acknowledgment of lineage is revocable by rejection. Understanding this principle is key to appreciating the Hanafi position on lineage claims.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
State the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the boy's lineage when Zayd denies paternity after the claimant initially said 'he is Zayd's son' and then 'he is my son'.
The ruling is that the boy does not become the claimant's son.
2
Identify the opposing view
Identify the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). What do they hold regarding the boy's lineage when Zayd denies?
According to them, the boy becomes the son of the person in whose custody he is.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is the basis for the Sahibayn's view? How do they argue that denial does not prevent the claim?
They treat the acknowledgment as binding unless the acknowledged party affirms, but here Zayd denies, so the acknowledgment remains.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does Abu Hanifa rebut this using the principle of revocability by rejection? Explain the analogy with the buyer acknowledging freeing and with li'an.
The key is that lineage acknowledgments are revocable by the denial of the acknowledged party, similar to revocable contracts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn?
Under Abu Hanifa, lineage is not established to the claimant; under the Sahibayn, it is established to the custodian.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال لصبي معه : هو ابن زيد، ثم قال : هو ابني، لم يكن ابنه، وكذا بعد كتابةِ الولد ورهنه... الخ، لكنّه سهو كذا في «حاشية العلامة الشامي على الدر» قوله : لم يكن ابنه ; لا حالاً ولا استقبالاً ، أما حالاً فظاهر ؛ لوجود المانع هو تعلق حق مثلاً الغير وأما استقبالاً ؛ فلان زيد إما أن يصدّقه أو يكذبه، أو يسكت عن التصديق والتكذيب، ففي الوجه الأول والثالث : لا تصح دعوته بالاتفاق ؛ لأنه لم ... وإن جَحَد زيد بنوته ) : هذا عند أبي حنيفة له ، وعندهما : إن جَحَدَ زِيدٌ بنوتَهُ يصير ابناً للذي في يدِهِ الصَّبيَّ؛ لأن الإقرار في النسب يرتدُ بالرَّد ... يتصل بإقراره تكذيب من جهة المقرّ له فبقي إقراره، وفي الوجه الثاني لم تصح دعوته عند الإمام، خلافاً لهما لما صرح به الشارح . قوله : وإن جحد زيد بنوته ; كلمة : إنّ وصليّة ؛ أي لا يثبت نسب ذلك الصبي إن لم يجحد زيد، وإن جحد فلا يثبت أيضاً ، وفائدة إن الوصلية أن يكون نقيضه أولى بالحكم من المذكور، والمذكور صورة الجحود، ونقيضه صورة عدم الجحود، فكان صورة عدم الجحود أولى؛ لعدم ثبوت النسب، ففيه الاتفاق، وفي المذكور خلاف كما عرفت. قوله : لأن الإقرار في النسب.... الخ ؛ تفصيلُه : إن إقراره بطل مجحود المقر له، فصار كأن لم يقرّ ; ولهذا أعتق عليه بدعوته لو كان عبداً له، والسر فيه : أن الإقرار بالنسب مما يرتدّ بالردّ ، إذ الإقرار بما لا يحتمل النقض يلحق بالإقرار بما يحتمل النقض ؛ ولهذا يعمل فيه الإكراه والهزل. فإنَّ من أكره على الطلاق والعتاق ففعل يقعُ الطلاق والعتاق، ولو أكره على الإقرار بهما فأقرّ لا يقع، كما لو أكره على البيع وغيره مما يحتمل النقض ففعل لا يثبت ، فإذا ثبت بأن الإقرار بما لا يحتمل النقض ثبت أنه يرتد بالرد. فصار كما إذا أقر المشتري على البائع بإعتاق من اشتراه ، فكذبه البائع، ثم قال : أنا أعتقته، يتحول إليه الولاء، ويرتد الإقرار به، والمقرّ له فكذا بهذا ; ولأنّ إقراره له بالنسب نفي، كنسب عن نفسه، وإنكار لوجوب الحقوق عليه، وذلك لا يمنع الإقرار به بعده ، بأن قال : ليس هو ابني، ثم قال : هو ابني، فكذا هذا. ألا ترى أنه يصح إكذاب الملاعنة عن نفسه بعد نفي النسب، بخلاف ما إذا صدق العبد المولى، حيث لا يصح فيه دعوى المولى؛ لأنَّ المقر يدعي بعد تصديق المقر له إياه نسباً ثابتاً من الغير، وبخلاف ما إذا لم يصدقه ولم يكذبه، حيث لا يصح فيه دعوة المولى أيضاً ؛ لأنه تعلق به حق المقرّ له على اعتبار تصديقه فيصير كولد الملاعنة لا يثبت نسبه من غير الملاعن لتعلق حقه به بتكذيب نفسه.
And if he said about a boy with him: 'He is the son of Zayd', then said: 'He is my son', he is not his son, and similarly after writing of the child and pawning him... etc., but it is an oversight as in the Hashiya of al-Allama al-Shami on al-Dur. His statement: 'he is not his son'; neither presently nor in the future. As for the present, it is apparent due to the existence of the impediment, which is the attachment of a right of another, for example. As for the future, because Zayd either affirms him or denies him, or remains silent regarding affirmation and denial. In the first and third cases, his claim is not valid by consensus, because he... And if Zayd denies his paternity: this, according to Abu Hanifa, is for him; and according to them (the two: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if Zayd denies his paternity, the boy becomes a son for the one in whose hand the boy is, because acknowledgment in lineage is revocable by rejection... a denial from the acknowledged party attaches to his acknowledgment, so his acknowledgment remains. In the second case, his claim is not valid according to the Imam, contrary to them, as the commentator stated. His statement: 'And if Zayd denies his paternity'; the word 'in' is wasliyya; meaning the lineage of that boy is not established if Zayd does not deny, and if he denies it is also not established. The benefit of the wasliyya is that its opposite is more deserving of the ruling than the mentioned. The mentioned is the case of denial, and its opposite is the case of non-denial. So the case of non-denial is more deserving of non-establishment of lineage, so there is consensus on it, and in the mentioned there is dispute as you know. His statement: 'because acknowledgment in lineage... etc.'; its detail: His acknowledgment is voided by the denial of the acknowledged party, so it becomes as if he did not acknowledge; and for this reason, if he were his slave, he would be freed by his claim. The secret behind it is that acknowledgment of lineage is revocable by rejection; because what is not susceptible to revocation is attached to what is susceptible to revocation; for this reason, duress and jest take effect in it. Indeed, whoever is coerced into divorce and freeing and does so, the divorce and freeing occur; but if he is coerced into acknowledging them and acknowledges, it does not occur, just as if he is coerced into sale and other things that are susceptible to revocation and does so, it is not established. So when it is established that what is not susceptible to revocation, it is established that it is revocable by rejection. So it becomes like the case where the buyer acknowledged upon the seller the freeing of the one he bought, then the seller denied him, then said: 'I freed him', the wala' reverts to him and the acknowledgment is revoked. So likewise in this case. And because his acknowledgment of lineage for him is a denial of lineage from himself and a denial of the obligation of rights upon him, and that does not prevent acknowledgment after it, as if he said: 'He is not my son', then said: 'He is my son'. So likewise this. Do you not see that it is valid for the one who performed li'an to deny lineage from himself after negation of lineage, contrary to the case where the slave affirms the master, where the master's claim is not valid; because the acknowledger claims, after the affirmation of the acknowledged, a lineage established from another. And contrary to the case where he neither affirms nor denies, where the master's claim is also not valid; because the right of the acknowledged attaches to him in consideration of his affirmation, so he becomes like the child of li'an, whose lineage is not established from someone other than the one who performed li'an, because his right is attached to him by his own denial of himself.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a person says of a boy with him 'he is Zayd's son' and later says 'he is my son'. The ruling is that the boy does not become his son, neither in the present nor in the future. The commentary explains three scenarios regarding Zayd's response: affirmation, denial, or silence. In affirmation and silence, the claim is invalid by consensus because the claimant's acknowledgment is contradicted or not established. In denial, there is a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the boy does not become the claimant's son, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the boy becomes the son of the person in whose hand he is. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view is that acknowledgment of lineage is revocable by rejection (يرتد بالرد). The commentary elaborates that since acknowledgment of lineage is an act that can be nullified by the denial of the acknowledged party, it is similar to the case where a buyer acknowledges a freeing, the seller denies it, and then the seller claims the freeing himself—the wala' reverts. Analogies are drawn with duress in divorce and freeing, and with the case of li'an (mutual imprecation), where a husband can retract his denial of paternity under certain conditions.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or confession, especially of lineage or a right.
ردّ (radd): Rejection or denial that nullifies an acknowledgment.
الملاعنة (al-mulā'anah): Mutual imprecation (li'an) between spouses when husband accuses wife of adultery and denies paternity of child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the secret (al-sirr) behind the ruling that acknowledgment of lineage is revocable by rejection?
A) Because duress and jest affect it.
B) Because it is attached to what is susceptible to revocation.
C) Because the acknowledged party's denial frees the slave.
D) Because it is like li'an.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an acknowledgment of lineage is nullified by the denial of the acknowledged party, following the principle that lineage is revocable by rejection.

The Child of the Deceived Man: Free in Origin, Compensated by Value
Explaining the child's freedom and valuation with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the child of the deceived man is free but compensable by monetary value, and evaluate the contrary view attributed to Umar.

Core Idea
The child of the deceived man is free in origin, but the father compensates the true owner by market value, not by a like-for-like slave.

Welcome. This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah deals with a complex scenario: a man marries or buys a woman in good faith, she bears his child, then the woman is claimed by her true owner. What is the status of the child? The Hanafi school, relying on consensus and qiyas, rules that the child is free but the father must pay its value. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the dispute with early authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal situation? The father (al-maghrur) had intercourse based on a valid claim, the woman later claimed. The child is born. Ruling: child is free (hurr al-asl) but father must pay compensation.
2
Locate the evidence for freedom
Consensus among the first generation and jurists that the child is free in origin. The text states 'لا خلاف بين الصدر الأول وفقهاء الأمصار أنه حر الأصل'.
This ijma establishes the child's intrinsic freedom.
3
Identify the dispute on compensation
The Salaf agree the father must compensate but differ on how: Umar said like-for-like slave, Ali (or another) said monetary value. Hanafis adopt value.
Thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in compensation method.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Qiyas: animals are not compensable by like, so humans are more so. Also reinterpretation of Umar's statement as 'value'.
Dalil: 'الحيوان لا يكون مضموناً بالمثل'.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under Hanafi view, father pays cash value; under opposing view, he must surrender a slave of same age/gender.
The Hanafi view avoids hardship and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(فإن مات الولد فلا شيء على أبيه) ؛ لعدم المنع منه (1) قوله : لأن ولد المغرور ... الخ ؛ حاصل الاستدلال : إنَّ هذا الولد ولد المغرور، وولد المغرور حر بالقيمة ، أما كونه ولد المغرور فلأن المغرور من يطأ امرأة معتمداً على ملك يمين أو نكاح فتلد منه ثم تستحق. أما كون ولد المغرور حراً بالقيمة ؛ فلأنه لا خلاف بين الصدر الأول وفقهاء الأمصار أنه حر الأصل، ولا خلاف أيضاً بين السلف أنه مضمون على الأبِ إِلا أَنَّ السلف اختلفوا في كيفية ضمانه : فقال عمر : يفك الغلام بالغلام والجارية بالجارية : يعني إن كان الولد غلاماً فعلى الأب غلام مثله، وإن كان جارية فعليه جارية مثلها. وقال عليه : عليه قيمة الولد، وإليه ذهب أصحابنا ؛ لأنه قد ثبت بالنص أنَّ الحيوان لا يكون مضموناً بالمثل. وتأويل حديث عمر : يفك الغلام بقيمة الغلام، والجارية بقيمة الجارية، فارتفع الخلاف، ولأنه مغرور، والأمة ملك المستحق، والولد جاءَ فاستوجب المستحق النظر إليه، والمغرور معذور، وقد بنى الأمر على سبب صحيح، فوجب الجمع بين النظرين مهما أمكن، وذلك بجعل الولد حرّ الأصل في حق الأب، ورقيقاً في حق المستحق ؛ لأنَّ استحقاق الأصل سبب استحقاق الجزء ، فيضمن قيمته يوم الخصومة. (2) قوله : وتعتبر قيمة الولد يوم الخصومة ؛ لأنه يوم المنع والتحوّل من العين إلى القيمة ؛ لأنه لما علق رقيقاً في حق المولى كان حقه في عين الولد، وإنما يتحوّل إلى القيمة بالقضاء، فتعتبر قيمته وقت التحوّل. [٣] قوله : لعدم المنع ؛ لأنه لو كان مملوكاً للمستحق حقيقة لم يكن مضموناً عليه، فإن ولد المغصوب أمانة عندنا كما تقرر في موضعه، فأولى أن لا يكون مضموناً عليه مع عدم الملك حقيقة.  كتاب الدعوى باب دعوى النسب ( وتركته له ) ؛ لأنَّه حُرُّ الأصل، فإن قتله أبوه أو غيرُهُ غُرِّمَ الأب قيمته ، ورجَعَ بها كثمنها على بائعه لا بالعقر)، إن قتلَهُ الأب يضمن قيمته للمستحق، وكذا إن قتلَهُ غيرُه ، فأخذ الأب ديته ، فإن الدِّيةَ بدلّ له، فسلامة البدل للأب كسلامة الولد ، ثُمَّ مَنْعُ البدلِ من المستحق كمنع الولد، وفيه القيمة، ويرجع بقيمته على البائع كما يرجع بثمنها ، ولا يرجعُ بالعقر الذي أَخَذَ منه المستحق ؛ لأنه بدلُ استيفاء منفعة البضع. (1) قوله : لأنه حر الأصل ؛ يعني في حق أبيه فيرثه أبوه، لا يقال : إنّ هذا الولد كما هو حر في حق أبيه كذلك رقيق في حق مدعيه ، فَلِمَ لم يقسم تركته بينهما ؛ لأنا نقول: هو حر في حق مدعيه أيضاً، ألا ترى أن ولاءه ليس لمدعيه، وإنما جعلناه رقيقاً في حقه ضرورة القضاء له بالقيمة، وكلُّ ما ثبت بالضرورة يتقدر بقدرها. [٢]قوله : فأخذ الأب ديته ؛ قيّد بالأخذ ، ذكر في «المبسوط» فإن قضى له بالدية فلم يقبضها لم يأخذ بالقيمة ؛ لأنَّ المنع لا يتحقق فيما لم يصل إلى يدها من البدل، فإنَّ قبض من الدية قدر قيمة المقتول قضى عليه بالقيمة للمستحق؛ لأنَّ المنع يتحقق بوصول يده إلى البدل، فيكون منعُهُ قدر قيمة الولد، كمنعه للولد. كذا في «الكفاية»). [٣]قوله : ويرجع ... الخ ؛ يعني ويرجع المشتري على أبيه بقيمة الولد التي ضمنها ، لأنَّ البيع كما يرجع المشتري بثمن الجارية ؛ لأنه صار كفيلا بما شرط عليه من البدل ؛ مبني على مساواة البدلين في حكم الضمان، فلما كان الثمن من جانب المشتري سالماً للبائع وجب أن يكون المبيع سالماً للمشتري. وذلك بأن يجعل البائع كفيلاً بسبب تملك البدل، فصار كأنه قال للمشتري : إنَّ الحكم قد ثبت لك، فإن ضَمِنَك أحدٌ بدعوى باطل فأنا ضامن لك بما ضَمِنَك ؛ ولأنَّ البائع التزم سلامتها عن العيب إذ المعاوضة تقتضي ذلك ، ولا عيب فوق الاستحقاق عليه.
(If the child dies, nothing is owed on his father) because there is no prevention (from the father). (1) His saying: "Because the child of the deceived man... etc."; the gist of the inference: This child is the child of the deceived man, and the child of the deceived man is free with a value. As for it being the child of the deceived man, the deceived man is one who has intercourse with a woman relying on ownership of a right hand or a marriage, and she gives birth from him, then she is claimed. As for the child of the deceived man being free with a value: because there is no disagreement among the first generation and the jurists of the regions that it is free in origin, and there is no disagreement among the predecessors that it is guaranteed upon the father, except that the predecessors differed in the manner of its guarantee: 'Umar said: 'A boy for a boy, a girl for a girl,' meaning if the child is a boy, then the father owes a similar boy; if a girl, then a similar girl. And it is said from him: 'Upon him is the value of the child,' and that is the position of our companions; because it is established by text that an animal is not guaranteed by a like. And the interpretation of the hadith of 'Umar is: 'A boy for the value of a boy, a girl for the value of a girl,' so the disagreement is resolved. And because he is deceived, the slave woman is the property of the claimant, the child came, and the claimant deserved to look to him, and the deceived is excused, and he based the matter on a valid cause, so it became necessary to combine both considerations whenever possible, and that is by making the child free in origin with respect to the father, and a slave with respect to the claimant; because entitlement to the origin is a cause for entitlement to the part, so he guarantees its value on the day of litigation. (2) His saying: "And the value of the child is considered on the day of litigation" because it is the day of prevention and transfer from the specific thing to the value; because when it was attached as a slave with respect to the master, his right was in the specific child, and it transfers to value only by judicial decision, so its value is considered at the time of transfer. [3] His saying: "Because there is no prevention" because if it were actually owned by the claimant, it would not be guaranteed for him; for the child of a usurped (woman) is a trust according to us, as established in its place, so it is more appropriate that it not be guaranteed for him in the absence of actual ownership. [PAGE_229] The Book of Claims, Chapter of Claiming Lineage (And his estate belongs to him) because he is free in origin; so if his father or someone else kills him, the father is liable for his value, and he recovers it as its price from his seller, not by the 'uqr (dower). If the father kills him, he guarantees his value to the claimant; likewise if someone else kills him, and the father takes his blood money, because the blood money is a substitute for him, so the safety of the substitute for the father is like the safety of the child, then preventing the substitute from the claimant is like preventing the child, and the value is in it, and he recovers its value from the seller just as he recovers its price, and he does not recover the 'uqr which the claimant took from him, because it is a substitute for the utilization of the usufruct of the vulva. (1) His saying: "Because he is free in origin" means with respect to his father, so his father inherits from him. It should not be said: This child, just as he is free with respect to his father, is also a slave with respect to his claimant, so why is his estate not divided between them? For we say: He is also free with respect to his claimant; do you not see that his patronage (wala') is not for his claimant? We only made him a slave with respect to him out of necessity for awarding him the value, and everything established by necessity is limited to its extent. [2] His saying: "So the father takes his blood money" is restricted to taking. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut: If he is awarded the blood money but does not receive it, he does not take the value; because prevention is not realized in what has not reached his hand of the substitute. If he receives from the blood money an amount equal to the value of the killed person, he is adjudged the value for the claimant; because prevention is realized by his hand reaching the substitute, so his prevention of that amount equals the value of the child, like his prevention of the child. Thus in al-Kifaya. [3] His saying: "And he recovers... etc." means the buyer recovers from his father the value of the child which he guaranteed, because the sale is like the buyer recovering the price of the slave girl; because he became a guarantor for what was stipulated upon him of the substitute, based on the equality of the two substitutes in the ruling of guarantee. So when the price from the buyer's side was safe for the seller, it is necessary that the sold item be safe for the buyer. That is by making the seller a guarantor due to his ownership of the substitute, so it is as if he said to the buyer: 'The ruling has been established for you; if someone claims against you with a false claim, I am a guarantor for you for what he claims against you.' And because the seller obligated the safety of the slave girl from defect, since the exchange requires that, and there is no defect greater than entitlement.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah examines the legal status of a child born to a woman who is later discovered to be owned by someone else (the case of al-maghrur, the deceived man). The commentator explains that if the child dies before any claim, the father owes nothing because there was no act of prevention. The core ruling is that the child is free (hurr al-asl) but the father must pay its value to the true owner. The commentator first establishes that the child is the deceived man's child because he had a valid cause (ownership or marriage). Then he proves the child's freedom: there is consensus among early Muslims and later jurists that the child is free in origin, and the father is liable for its value. The dispute among the Salaf was about the method: Umar reportedly said 'a boy for a boy, a girl for a girl' (like-for-like), while Ali (or another) said 'value'. The Hanafis adopt the value position based on qiyas: since animals are not compensated by like, humans are more so. They reinterpret Umar's statement to mean value. The valuation is at the time of litigation because that is when the right transforms from the child itself to monetary compensation. The father's liability arises from his prevention of the owner's access. The passage also covers inheritance: the child inherits from the father and vice versa because the child is free in relation to him. If the father or another kills the child, the father must pay the value to the owner. The father can then recover that amount from the seller (the one who sold the woman) as part of the sale price, but he cannot recover the 'uqr (compensation for usufruct) because that was for the benefit received. The commentator addresses objections: why not divide the child's estate between father and claimant? Because the child is also free in relation to the claimant, but was deemed a slave only for the purpose of valuation by necessity.

Key Terms
المغرور (al-maghrur): A man who has intercourse with a woman relying on a valid claim of ownership (by purchase or marriage) but later discovers she belongs to someone else.
ولد المغرور (walad al-maghrur): The child born to the deceived man from such a woman; it is free in origin but the father must pay its value to the true owner.
قيمة يوم الخصومة (qimat yawm al-khusuma): The market value of the child assessed on the day the legal claim (khusuma) is made, i.e., the date of litigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At what time is the value of the child (walad al-maghrur) assessed according to the Hanafi school?
A) At the time of the child's birth
B) At the time of the father's death
C) At the time of litigation (yawm al-khusuma)
D) At the time the woman is claimed

Key Takeaway
The child of the deceived man is free in origin; the father compensates the owner by paying market value at the time of litigation, not by surrendering a like slave.
